good time watching this.
Android is a Hell of a lot less strict about people actually using their phones. It's a personal mobile device, where Apple always has certain restrictions kept in place that makes it feel corporate and boring. At least their phones run well... I guess It's why so many people stay on Android. Because those phones allow you to have full customization on your phone. Be allowed to fully change the font that's shown, have images set up on your keyboard, completely change all app icons on a whim, you can do anything with an Android. Apple just allows you to change from light to dark, and... I guess have preset ringtones. That's it. For the context of this video, the Play Store basically says "Yeah, do whatever, we do not care." You can upload whatever you want onto the Play Store thanks to it using a .apk file structure, where Apple has all apps under extensive review so you don't upload garbage (which isn't the case anymore, thanks shotty mobile game template). Because of that, all the bootleg Crash games are on Android. I'm assuming there aren't many console releases with those NES bootleg systems, likely because of the spin. I mean, without it, it's not even Crash. Most of those games are simply just putting a character in a specific bad game and calling it a day, which is why I mention that. And there isn't really any NES game where you spin to break stuff, so... yeah.  I'm pretty sure a big reason why a majority of them didn't even open is because they were made on much older versions of Android. It's a common problem almost every shotty-game on the Play Store goes through because they've been sitting there with cobwebs piling up for YEARS as the "devs" just kinda stopped caring. I'm sure they didn't care at all when they uploaded them given the quality... yeesh.

The reason that the Google Play store is the one with all the bootlegs is because when making a game in unity, putting it on IOS takes forever and might not even happen even after doing everything required. Meanwhile, if itâ€™s a game and you have a Google account then you can put a game on Google Play. With Nintendo and Sega and what not itâ€™s a lot more shit to go through with copyright lawsuits and manufacturing physical copies and making a game using that specific devices dev kits and hardware, making it damn near impossible to make a knockoff bootleg game, unless itâ€™s easier to get away with copyright theft in your country and if you have easier access to a Gameboy or Genesis Dev Kit. Donâ€™t get me wrong, there are plenty of bootleg knock offs on IOS and Console and even Steam sometimes, itâ€™s just so much harder to get away with stealing a million dollar companies IP with those ways, and itâ€™s impossible to either Develop the game to begin with, or put the game onto the store in general.

15:38 I find it funny that those issues appear in this game because they normally only appear in NES games where the camera can move diagonally. Those graphical issues on the right edge are the result of the game I think de-loading tiles as the camera moves away from them, or maybe they're just being moved to where they'll be used next, I don't know what the game is actually doing with those tiles. What's important is that basically every game with scrolling of any kind on the system, and likely most 8 and 16-bit systems for that matter, does this, but you don't see it in games like the original Super Mario Bros. or Metroid because they use an offscreen buffer to push it beyond the viewable area.   However, the NES is only capable of applying this to one axis at a time; that obviously isn't a problem for a game like SMB1 that only ever scrolls on one axis anyway, and while Metroid does scroll on both axes, it never does so at the same time, so the game can move the offscreen buffer to where it needs to be for that specific room. However, games like Super Mario Bros. 3 and Kirby's Adventure can scroll diagonally, which means that the game is now scrolling on both axes, if it wasn't obvious. Since you can't apply the offscreen buffer to both axes, the programmers had to choose one to apply it to.  TL;DR: Those graphical issues on the edge of the screen usually only appear on NES games with diagonal scrolling since the system can apply an offscreen buffer to one axis at a time. The Reason I find it funny that these issues exist in this game is that judging by the footage, it doesn't even appear to scroll vertically at all, only horizontal; if this is true, then that means they most likely didn't apply an offscreen buffer at all.

26:30 this isnt even a port of the psp version. it is the psp version. The program is actually a popular psp emulator called ppsspp and it has its initial menu disabled, instead directed straight to the iso (game file) it downloads of the game.  The "developer" (if you can even call them that) just took an existing program used to run psp games and made an app on the store that downloads the game file (most likely pirated), downloads the emulator, and says that its an original product.

15:38  Actually those glitchy-looking tiles scrolling in from the right like that are the result of NES hardware limitations (which also get recreated in emulation), not from a game running poorly. NES games have a very limited tile space to work with due to the hardware they were developed for, so they were designed with the far tiles allowing the screen to wrap over and overwrite stuff as it entered the frame.  Devs never bothered to fix it because TVs at the time of the NES didn't show you all the pixels, so those "glitchy" tiles at the far end were never visible to the average NES player until TVs that displayed pixel-perfect images started becoming the norm.  Semi-relatedly, this far-edge pixel cutoff area is why Ocarina of Time had that one dungeon entrance map icon mysteriously floating at the top left of the screen for seemingly no reason in every rerelease that nobody ever saw on the original N64.

My condolences about that trip not paying off and the injury.  There is however, a fun fact about that Game Boy Advance bootleg. It is the far buggier version of an asset flip, of a downgraded port, of a SNES Digimon Bootleg, that was already clunky and buggy. That specific bootleg game has been asset flipped so many times it's been a Mario game, a Sonic game ( The infamous Sonic 3 Fighter Sonic one ), a TMNT game, a Rayman game, and even stuff like an Ultraman game. All of them are bad and don't even have the amount of content the SNES "original" had. These ones are obviously derided by bootleg enthusiasts as well due to the laziness and shoddiness of it all.
